cty.NullVal(cty.DynamicPseudoType),\n391: \t\t\t\tAfter:  cty.NullVal(cty.DynamicPseudoType),\n392: \t\t\t},\n393: \t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n394: \t\t}\n395: \t\treturn noop, nil\n396: \t}\n397: \n398: \tunmarkedPriorVal, _ := currentState.Value.UnmarkDeep()\n399: \n400: \t// The config and new value are null to signify that this is a destroy\n401: \t// operation.\n402: \tnullVal := \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n410: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n411: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n412: \t\treturn plan, diags\n413: \t}\n414: \n415: \tvar resp consulting the provider previously.\n419: \t\t// We can just set the planned state to deleted without consulting the\n420: \t\t// provider.\n421: \t\tresp = providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse{\n422: \t\t\tPlannedState: nullVal,\n423: \t\t}\n424: \t} else {\n425: \t\t// Allow the provider to check the destroy plan, and insert any\n426: \t\t// necessary private data.\n427: \t\tresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n428: \t\t\tTypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n429: \t\t\tConfig:           nullVal,\n430: \t\t\tPriorState: have a config for all destroys, but we want to reference\n437: \t\t// it in the diagnostics if we do.\n438: \t\tif n.Config != nil {\n439: \t\t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n440: \t\t}\n441: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n442: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n443: \t\t\treturn plan, diags\n444: \t\t}\n445: \n446: \t\t// Check that the provider returned a null value here, since that is the\n447: \t\t// only valid value for a destroy plan.\n448: \t\tif !resp.PlannedState.IsNull() {\n449: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n450: \t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n451: \t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n452: \t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n453: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned a non-null destroy value for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n454: \t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr),\n455: \t\t\t),\n456: \t\t\t)\n457: \t\t\treturn plan, diags\n458: \t\t}\n459: \t}\n460: \n461: \t// Plan is always the same for a destroy.\n462: \tplan = &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n463: \t\tAddr:        absAddr,\n464: \t\tPrevRunAddr: n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n465: \t\tDeposedKey:  deposedKey,\n466: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n467: \t\t\tAction: plans.Delete,\n468: \t\t\tBefore: currentState.Value,\n469: \t\t\tAfter:  nullVal,\n470: \t\t},\n471: \t\tPrivate:      resp.PlannedPrivate,\n472: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n473: \t}\n474: \n475: \treturn plan, diags\n476: }\n477: \n478: // planForget returns a Forget change.\n479: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planForget(ctx EvalContext, currentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n480: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n481: \tvar plan *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n482: \n483: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n484: \n485: \t// If there is no state or our attributes object is null then the resource\n486: \t// is already removed.\n487: \tif currentState == nil || currentState.Value.IsNull() {\n488: \t\t// We still need to generate a \t\tAddr:        absAddr,\n512: \t\tPrevRunAddr: n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n513: \t\tDeposedKey:  deposedKey,\n514: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n515: \t\t\tAction: plans.Forget,\n516: \t\t\tBefore: currentState.Value,\n517: \t\t\tAfter:  nullVal,\n518: \t\t},\n519: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n520: \t}\n521: \n522: \treturn plan, diags\n523: }\n524: \n525: // writeChange saves a planned change for an instance object into the set of\n526: // global planned changes.\n527: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) writeChange(ctx EvalContext, change *plans.ResourceInstanceChange, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n528: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n529: \n530: \tif change == nil {\n531: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n532: \t\t// the set of changes.\n533: \t\tchanges.RemoveResourceInstanceChange(n.Addr, deposedKey)\n534: \t\treturn nil\n535: \t}\n536: \n537: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n538: \tif err != nil {\n539: \t\treturn err\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif change.Addr.String() != n.Addr.String() || change.DeposedKey != deposedKey {\n543: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n544: \t\tpanic(\"inconsistent address and/or deposed key in writeChange\")\n545: \t}\n546: \tif change.PrevRunAddr.Resource.Resource.Type == \"\" {\n547: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n548: \t\t// (The change.Encode function actually has its own fixup to just\n549: \t\t// quietly make this match change.Addr in the incorrect case, but we\n550: \t\t// intentionally panic here in order to catch incorrect callers where\n551: \t\t// the stack trace will hopefully be actually useful. The tolerance\n552: \t\t// at the next layer down is mainly to accommodate sloppy input in\n553: \t\t// older tests.)\n554: \t\tpanic(\"unpopulated ResourceInstanceChange.PrevRunAddr in writeChange\")\n555: \t}\n556: \n557: \tri := n.Addr.Resource\n558: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(ri.Resource)\n559: \tif schema == nil {\n560: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n561: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", ri.Resource.Type)\n562: \t}\n563: \n564: \tcsrc, err := change.Encode(schema.ImpliedType())\n565: \tif err != nil {\n566: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode planned changes for %s: %s\", n.Addr, err)\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tchanges.AppendResourceInstanceChange(csrc)\n570: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n571: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s\", change.Action, n.Addr)\n572: \t} else {\n573: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s deposed object %s\", change.Action, n.Addr, deposedKey)\n574: \t}\n575: \n576: \treturn nil\n577: }\n578: \n579: // refresh does a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n581: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n582: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n583: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n584: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s\", absAddr)\n585: \t} else {\n586: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s (deposed object %s)\", absAddr, deposedKey)\n587: \t}\n588: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n589: \tif err != nil {\n590: \t\treturn state, diags.Append(err)\n591: \t}\n592: \t// If we have no state, we don't do any refreshing\n593: \tif state == nil {\n594: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] refresh: %s: no state, so not refreshing\", absAddr)\n595: \t\treturn state, diags\n596: \t}\n597: \n598: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.Resource.ContainingResource())\n599: \tif schema == nil {\n600: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n601: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type))\n602: \t\treturn state, diags\n603: \t}\n604: \n605: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n606: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n607: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n608: \t\treturn state, diags\n609: \t}\n610: \n611: \t// Call pre-refresh hook\n612: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n613: \t\treturn h.PreRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, state.Value)\n614: \t}))\n615: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n616: \t\treturn state, diags\n617: \t}\n618: \n619: \t// Refresh!\n620: \tpriorVal := state.Value\n621: \n622: \t// Unmarked before sending to provider\n623: \tvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\n624: \tif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n625: \t\tpriorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n626: \t}\n627: \n628: \tvar resp providers.ReadResourceResponse\n629: \tif n.override != nil {\n630: \t\t// If we have an override set for this resource, we don't want to talk\n631: \t\t// to the provider so we'll just return whatever was in state.\n632: \t\tresp = providers.ReadResourceResponse{\n633: \t\t\tNewState: priorVal,\n634: \t\t}\n635: \t} else {\n636: \t\tresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n637: \t\t\tTypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n638: \t\t\tPriorState: \t}\n651: \n652: \tif resp.NewState == cty.NilVal {\n653: \t\t// This ought not to happen in real cases since it's not possible to\n654: \t\t// send NilVal over the plugin RPC channel, but it can come up in\n655: \t\t// tests due to sloppy mocking.\n656: \t\tpanic(\"new state is cty.NilVal\")\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tif !resp.NewState.IsWhollyKnown() {\n660: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n661: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n662: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n663: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n664: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n665: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, \"The returned state contains unknown values\",\n666: \t\t\t),\n667: \t\t))\n668: \t}\n669: \n670: \tfor _, err := range resp.NewState.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n671: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n672: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n673: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n674: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n675: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n676: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, tfdiags.FormatError(err),\n677: \t\t\t),\n678: \t\t))\n679: \t}\n680: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n681: \t\treturn state, diags\n682: \t}\n683: \n684: \tnewState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)\n685: \tif !newState.RawEquals(resp.NewState) {\n686: \t\t// We had to fix up this object in some way, and we still need to\n687: \t\t// for %q during refresh\\n\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tret := state.DeepCopy()\n693: \tret.Value = newState\n694: \tret.Private = resp.Private\n695: \n696: \t// We have no way to exempt provider using the legacy SDK from this check,\n697: \t// so we can only log inconsistencies with the updated state values.\n698: \t// In most cases these are not errors anyway, and represent \"drift\" from\n699: \t// external changes which will be handled by the subsequent plan.\n700: \tif errs := objchange.AssertObjectCompatible(schema, priorVal, ret.Value); len(errs) > 0 \t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n704: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n705: \t\t}\n706: \t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n707: \t}\n708: \n709: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n710: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n711: \t\treturn h.PostRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, priorVal, ret.Value)\n712: \t}))\n713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n714: \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n737: \tif err != nil {\n738: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(resource)\n742: \tif schema == nil {\n743: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n744: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", resource.Type))\n745: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n746: \t}\n747: \n748: \t// If we're importing and generating config, generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. There's\n792: \t// no need to re-plan this resource.\n793: \tif plannedChange != nil && plannedChange.Action == plans.NoOp {\n794: \t\treturn plannedChange, currentState.DeepCopy(), keyData, diags\n795: \t}\n796: \n797: \torigConfigVal, _, configDiags := ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n798: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n799: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n800: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n801: \t}\n802: \n803: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n804: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n805: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n806: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n807: \t}\n808: \n809: \tvar priorVal cty.Value\n810: \tvar priorValTainted cty.Value\n811: \tvar priorPrivate []byte\n812: \tif currentState != nil {\n813: \t\tif currentState.Status != states.ObjectTainted {\n814: \t\t\tpriorVal = currentState.Value\n815: \t\t\tpriorPrivate = currentState.Private\n816: \t\t} else {\n817: \t\t\t// If the prior state is tainted then we'll proceed below like\n818: \t\t\t// we're creating an entirely new object, but then turn it into\n819: \t\t\t// a synthetic \"Replace\" change at the end, creating the same\n820: \t\t\t// result as if the provider had marked at least one argument\n821: \t\t\t// change as \"requires replacement\".\n822: \t\t\tpriorValTainted = currentState.Value\n823: \t\t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t} else {\n826: \t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n827: \t}\n828: \n829: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Re-validating config for %q\", n.Addr)\n830: \t// Allow the provider to validate the final set of values.  The config was\n831: \t// statically validated early on, but there may have been unknown values\n832: \t// which the provider could not validate at the time.\n833: \t//\n834: \t// TODO: It would be more correct to validate the config after\n835: \t// ignore_changes has been applied, but the current implementation cannot\n836: \t// exclude computed-only attributes when given the `all` option.\n837: \n838: \t// we must unmark and use the original config, since the ignore_changes\n839: \t// handling below needs access to the marks.\n840: \tunmarkedConfigVal, _ := origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n841: \tvalidateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n842: \t\tproviders.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n843: \t\t\tTypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n844: \t\t\tConfig:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n845: \t\t},\n846: \t)\n847: \tdiags = diags.Append(validateResp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n848: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n849: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n850: \t}\n851: \n852: \t// ignore_changes is meant to only apply to the configuration, so it must\n853: \t// be applied before we generate a plan. Objects with this status\n1258: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1259: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1260: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1261: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1262: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1263: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1264: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1265: \t}\n1266: \n1267: \treturn plan, state, keyData, diags\n1268: }\n1269: \n1270: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1271: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1272: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1273: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1274: \t\treturn config, nil\n1275: \t}\n1276: \n1277: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1278: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1279: \n1280: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1281: \t\treturn config, nil\n1282: \t}\n1283: \n1284: \tif ignoreAll {\n1285: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1286: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1287: \t\t// config with computed values. \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A n.nestedInCheckBlock()\n1725: \tif nested {\n1726: \t\t// Going forward from this point, the only reason we will fail is\n1727: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1733: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1734: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1735: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1736: \t\t// success overall.\n1737: \t\t//\n1738: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1739: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1740: \t\t// to be StatusPass. The rest of this function will only update the\n1741: \t\t// status if it should be StatusFail.\n1742: \t\tdefer func() {\n1743: \t\t\tstatus := ctx.Checks().ObjectCheckStatus(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module))\n1744: \t\t\tif status == checks.StatusUnknown {\n1745: \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := configVal.IsWhollyKnown()\n1751: \tdepsPending := n.dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx)\n1752: \t// If our configuration contains any unknown values, or we depend on any\n1753: \t// unknown values then we must defer the read to the apply phase by\n1754: \t// producing a \"Read\" change for this resource, and a placeholder value for\n1755: \t// it in the state.\n1756: \tif depsPending || !configKnown {\n1757: \t\t// We can't plan any changes if we're only refreshing, so the only\n1758: \t\t// value we can set here is whatever was in state previously.\n1759: \t\tif skipPlanChanges {\n1760: \t\t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1761: \t\t\t\tValue:  priorVal,\n1762: \t\t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1763: \t\t\t}\n1764: \n1765: \t\t\treturn nil, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1766: \t\t}\n1767: \n1768: \t\tvar reason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1769: \t\tswitch {\n1770: \t\tcase !configKnown:\n1771: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration not fully known yet, so deferring to apply phase\", n.Addr)\n1772: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown\n1773: \t\tcase depsPending:\n1774: \t\t\t// NOTE: depsPending can be true at the same time as configKnown\n1775: \t\t\t// is false; configKnown takes precedence because it's more\n1776: \t\t\t// specific.\n1777: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration is fully known, at least one dependency has changes pending\", n.Addr)\n1778: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseDependencyPending\n1779: \t\t}\n1780: \n1781: \t\tunmarkedConfigVal, configMarkPaths := configVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n1782: \t\tproposedNewVal := objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1783: \t\tproposedNewVal = proposedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1784: \n1785: \t\t// Apply detects that the data source will need to be read by the After\n1786: \t\t// value containing unknowns from PlanDataResourceObject.\n1787: \t\tplannedChange := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1788: \t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1789: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1790: \t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1791: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1792: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1793: \t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1794: \t\t\t\tAfter:  proposedNewVal,\n1795: \t\t\t},\n1796: \t\t\tActionReason: reason,\n1797: \t\t}\n1798: \n1799: \t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1800: \t\t\tValue: addrs.NotDeposed, plans.Read, priorVal, proposedNewVal)\n1806: \t\t}))\n1807: \n1808: \t\treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1809: \t}\n1810: \n1811: \t// We have a complete configuration with no dependencies to wait on, so we\n1812: \t// can read the data source into the state.\n1813: \tnewVal, readDiags := n.readDataSource(ctx, configVal)\n1814: \n1815: \t// Now we've loaded the data, and diags tells us whether we were successful\n1816: \t// or not, we are going to create our plannedChange and our\n1817: \t// proposedNewState.\n1818: \tvar plannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n1819: \tvar plannedNewState *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n1820: \n1821: \t// If we are a nested block, then we want to create a plannedChange that\n1822: \t// tells \t// disguise that for a nested block. So,\n1835: \t\t// if we encountered an error we'll tidy up newVal so it makes sense\n1836: \t\t// and handle the error. If so, this resource will be loaded during both plan and apply\n1891: // operations to make sure the check is always giving the latest information.\n1892: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) nestedInCheckBlock() (*configs.Check, bool) {\n1893: \tif n.Config.Container != nil {\n1894: \t\tcheck, ok := n.Config.Container.(*configs.Check)\n1895: \t\treturn check, ok\n1896: \t}\n1897: \treturn nil, false\n1898: }\n1899: \n1900: // dependenciesHavePendingChanges determines whether any managed resource the\n1901: // receiver depends on has a change pending in the plan, in which case we'd\n1902: // need to override the usual behavior of immediately reading from the data\n1903: // source where possible, and instead defer the read until the apply step.\n1904: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx EvalContext) bool {\n1905: \tnModInst := n.Addr.Module\n1906: \tnMod := nModInst.Module()\n1907: \n1908: \t// Check and see if any depends_on dependencies have\n1909: \t// changes, since they won't show up as changes in the\n1910: \t// configuration.\n1911: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n1912: \n1913: \tdepsToUse := n.dependsOn\n1914: \n1915: \tif n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1916: \t\tif n.Config.HasCustomConditions() {\n1917: \t\t\t// For a data resource with custom conditions we need to look at\n1918: \t\t\t// the full set of resource dependencies -- both direct and\n1919: \t\t\t// indirect -- because an upstream update might be what's needed\n1920: \t\t\t// in order to make a condition pass.\n1921: \t\t\tdepsToUse = n.Dependencies\n1922: \t\t}\n1923: \t}\n1924: \n1925: \tfor _, d := range depsToUse {\n1926: \t\tif d.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1927: \t\t\t// Data sources have no external side effects, so they pose a need\n1928: \t\t\t// to delay this read. main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx evalApplyProvisioners determines if provisioners need to be run, and if so\n2056: // executes the provisioners for a resource and returns an updated error if\n2057: // provisioning fails.\n2058: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2060: \n2061: \tif state == nil {\n2062: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s has no state, so skipping provisioners\", n.Addr)\n2063: \t\treturn nil\n2064: \t}\n2065: \tif when == configs.ProvisionerWhenCreate && !createNew {\n2066: \t\t// If we're not creating a new resource, then don't run provisioners\n2067: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] []*configs.Provisioner {\n2108: \t// Fast path the zero case\n2109: \tif config == nil || config.Managed == nil {\n2110: \t\treturn nil\n2111: \t}\n2112: \n2113: \tif len(config.Managed.Provisioners) \t\tif p.When == when {\n2120: \t\t\tresult = append(result, p)\n2121: \t\t}\n2122: \t}\n2123: \n2124: \treturn result\n2125: }\n2126: \n2127: // applyProvisioners executes the provisioners for a resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the {\n2152: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] applyProvisioners: provisioning %s with %q\", n.Addr, prov.Type)\n2153: \n2154: \t\t// Get the provisioner\n2155: \t\tprovisioner, err := In practice not all remote\\n17: // objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,\\n18: // but this is the most common case.\\n19: //\\n20: // It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.\\n21: // Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.\\n22: type ResourceInstanceObject struct {\\n23: \\t// Value is the object-typed value representing the remote object within\\n24: \\t// Terraform.\\n25: \\tValue cty.Value\\n26: \\n27: \\t// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was\\n28: \\t// last created or updated. Terraform Core does not use this value in\\n29: \\t// any way and it is not exposed anywhere in the user interface, so\\n30: \\t// a provider can use it for retaining any necessary private state.\\n31: \\tPrivate []byte\\n32: \\n33: \\t// Status represents the \\\"readiness\\\" of the object as of the last time\\n34: \\t// it was updated.\\n35: \\tStatus ObjectStatus\\n36: \\n37: \\t// Dependencies is a set of absolute address to other resources this\\n38: \\t// instance dependeded on when it was applied. Since it cannot be moved into the\\n64: \\t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\\n65: \\tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\\n66: \\n67: \\t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\\n68: \\t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\\n69: \\t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\\n70: \\t//\\n71: \\t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\\n72: \\t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\\n73: \\t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. Now I can see the flow. Line 718-720:```go\n// Mark the value if necessaryif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}```\n\nSo after the refresh, the original marks from the state are re-applied!\n\nBut here's the critical issue: `priorPaths` only contains the marks that were in the original state's `AttrSensitivePaths` - which only has marks from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.\n\nSo here's what's happening:\n\n1. **During apply (when state is written):**\n   - The state is written with marks from sensitive variables\n   - Schema-sensitive marks are NOT written to state\n   - This is because marks are stripped by `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` during encoding\n\n2. **During refresh (in plan):**\n   - State is read: value has marks from sensitive variables\n   - Marks are extracted: `priorPaths` = marks from sensitive variables only\n   - Provider is called with unmarked value\n   - Provider returns new state without any marks\n   - Original marks from variables are re-applied to the refresh result\n   - But schema marks are NOT applied here!\n\n3. **During planning (plan method is called):**\n   - `priorVal` is the refreshed state value WITH marks from variables\n   - `priorPaths` are extracted from `priorVal` = marks from variables\n   - Provider plan is called with unmarked prior value\n   - Provider returns `plannedNewVal` with no marks\n   - At line 1208, it compares `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)` with `priorPaths`\n\n4. **The asymmetry:**\n   - When state is written to file: Only variable-reference marks are written (schema marks are lost)\n   - When state is read for evaluation via `GetResource()` in evaluate.go: Schema marks ARE applied\n   - When state is read for planning: Schema marks are NOT applied, so the planned value lacks schema-based sensitivity that should be there. This creates a mismatch where the plan doesn't capture all the sensitivity information that would be present during evaluation, leading to incorrect diff calculations when the plan is later used.\n\nThe core problem emerges in the comparison logic: when `terraform plan` reads state and compares values, it's missing schema-defined sensitive attributes. The check at line 1208 that determines whether to mark something as an Update relies on mark equality, but if schema marks aren't being applied during the read phase, the comparison becomes unreliable. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01494SEWi8rcYkZHD9FejWdx","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_017r7Cm5rr3fM13Fhu2eKQjf","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the refresh/plan cycle creates an asymmetry in sensitivity mark application. The provider schema's `Sensitive: true` attribute declarations are never persisted to state, causing the evaluator's compensating mark-application logic to create inconsistencies that trigger false \"Update\" actions when no values have actually changed.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **sensitivity mark gap** between three critical stages:\n\n1. **State Serialization** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): When state is written to disk, only sensitivity marks from variable references are saved in `AttrSensitivePaths`; schema-defined sensitive attributes are lost.\n\n2. **State Deserialization** (`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`): When state is read, marks are re-applied from the incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths`, lacking schema marks.\n\n3. **Evaluation-Time Compensation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`): The `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but this compensating layer is NOT applied during plan generation in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.\n\nThis asymmetry causes the plan phase to compare:\n- **Planned state** (from provider, no marks at all)\n- **Prior state** (from state file with incomplete marks, only from variables)\n\nWhen the marks differ even though values don't, a phantom \"Update\" action is triggered.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Sensitivity Marks Lost During State Encoding\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go`, lines 94-136\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Extract marks from value before serialization\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()  // Line 98\n\n    // Convert to JSON (loses all mark information)\n    src, err := ctyjson.Marshal(val, ty)       // Line 111\n\n    // Return object with incomplete marks\n    return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n        SchemaVersion:      schemaVersion,\n        AttrsJSON:          src,                // JSON has NO marks\n        AttrSensitivePaths: pvm,                // Only marks from variables\n        Private:            o.Private,\n        ...\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:** `pvm` (path-value marks) extracted at line 98 contains ONLY marks that were already on the value—which come from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations. The provider schema marks were never on the value in the first place because they're only applied during expression evaluation, not during state persistence.\n\n### 2. Incomplete Marks Re-Applied During State Decoding\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object_src.go`, lines 77-104\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    var val cty.Value\n    ...\n    val, err = ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n\n    // Re-apply marks from state (INCOMPLETE - missing schema marks)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Line 90\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe value is re-marked with `AttrSensitivePaths`, but these paths are incomplete—they lack any paths from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true`.\n\n### 3. Plan Comparison Without Schema Marks\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, lines 725-1250\n\nThe `plan()` method (called from `managedResourceExecute` at line 250 of `node_resource_plan_instance.go`) handles the plan phase:\n\n```go\n// Line 869: Extract marks from prior state (incomplete)\nunmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 871: Create proposed value\nproposedNewVal := objchange.ProposedNew(schema, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n\n// Line 902: Call provider (unmarked values sent)\nresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n    TypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    Config:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n    PriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,        // No schema marks\n    ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,          // No schema marks\n    ...\n})\n\n// Line 916: Provider response (no marks)\nplannedNewVal := resp.PlannedState\n\n// Line 1082: Compare unmarked values\neqV := unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)\neq := eqV.IsKnown() && eqV.True()\n\n// Line 1208: PHANTOM UPDATE TRIGGER\n// If values are equal but marks differ, mark as Update\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Flow:**\n- `priorPaths` contains marks extracted from the state value (line 869)\n- These marks only include marks from sensitive variable references\n- Schema-defined sensitive attributes are NOT in `priorPaths`\n- `plannedNewVal` comes from provider with NO marks\n- Mark comparison at line 1208 can trigger false positives if schema marks should be present\n\n### 4. Refresh Path Reapplies Incomplete Marks\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, lines 619-723\n\nThe refresh method (called during plan at line 208 of `node_resource_plan_instance.go`):\n\n```go\n// Line 620-626: Extract marks before provider call\npriorVal := state.Value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Line 636-641: Provider call (unmarked)\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    TypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    PriorState:   priorVal,      // Unmarked\n    Private:      state.Private,\n    ProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n})\n\n// Line 693: New state from provider\nret.Value = newState\n\n// Line 718-720: Reapply original marks (INCOMPLETE)\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Issue:** The marks reapplied at line 719 are incomplete because `priorPaths` lacks schema marks.\n\n### 5. Evaluator's Compensating Mark Application\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`, lines 541-725\n\nThe `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation:\n\n```go\n// Line 718-723: For regular state objects\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()           // Remove existing marks\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // Add schema marks\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Asymmetry:** This compensating mark application happens ONLY during expression evaluation via `GetResource()`, NOT during:\n- State decoding for planning\n- Provider calls during refresh/plan\n- Difference calculation\n\nThis creates an asymmetry where:\n- Values read FROM state for evaluation have schema marks (via `GetResource()`)\n- Values read FROM state during planning don't have schema marks\n- Planned values from provider have no marks at all\n\n### 6. JSON Output Manifestation\n\n**File:** `internal/command/jsonplan/resource.go`, line 44\n\nThe `SensitiveValues` field in JSON plan output reflects only the marks saved in state:\n\n```go\nSensitiveValues json.RawMessage `json:\"sensitive_values,omitempty\"`\n```\n\nThese are derived from state's `AttrSensitivePaths` (via the plan's change tracking), which lacks schema-defined sensitive paths. This produces incorrect `sensitive_values` in `terraform show -json` output.\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** - Encodes state, loses schema marks\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** - Decodes state, applies incomplete marks\n3. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** - Plan generation without schema marks\n   - `plan()` method (line 725+)\n   - `refresh()` method (line 580+)\n   - Mark comparison at line 1208\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** - Compensating schema mark application only during evaluation\n   - `GetResource()` method (line 541+)\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/`** - JSON output reflects incomplete sensitivity information\n6. **`internal/marks.go`** - Mark equality comparison (`marksEqual()`, `filterMarks()`)\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response Boundary:** Provider returns `ReadResource` / `PlanResourceChange` response with **no sensitivity marks** (providers don't mark values; Terraform does).\n\n2. **State Persistence Gap:** When state is encoded via `instance_object.Encode()`, only marks that are already on the value are persisted. Schema-defined sensitive marks were never on the value because they're only applied during expression evaluation, so they're lost forever.\n\n3. **Incomplete State Reading:** When state is decoded via `instance_object_src.Decode()`, the re-marked value only has marks from sensitive variable references (stored in `AttrSensitivePaths`), not from schema.\n\n4. **Plan Without Compensation:** During planning in `node_resource_abstract_instance.plan()`, the code:\n   - Extracts incomplete marks from prior state\n   - Calls provider with unmarked values\n   - Receives unmarked planned value from provider\n   - Compares marks at line 1208, detecting \"changes\" that are just missing schema marks\n\n5. **Evaluation-Time Asymmetry:** During expression evaluation (via `GetResource()` in evaluate.go), schema marks ARE applied, but only for expressions—not for plan comparison.\n\n6. **Phantom Diff Manifestation:** The plan detects a \"change\" (NoOp → Update at line 1209) because:\n   - The planned value has no marks\n   - The prior value has only variable-reference marks\n   - Schema marks are absent from both, but the comparison logic doesn't know they should be there\n\n7. **JSON Output Inaccuracy:** When the plan is serialized to JSON or state, `sensitive_values` reflects only variable-reference sensitivity, omitting schema-defined sensitive attributes.\n\n---\n\n## Diagnostic Evidence\n\n**When phantom updates occur:**\n- `terraform plan` immediately after `terraform apply` shows \"will be updated in-place\"\n- `terraform show -json` shows incomplete `sensitive_values` lacking schema-marked attributes\n- `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes\n- The phantom diff disappears if no provider-schema attributes are marked `Sensitive: true`\n\n**Root Cause Signature:**\n- State file's `sensitive_attributes` lists only paths from variable references\n- Missing paths for all schema-defined `Sensitive: true` attributes\n- Plan comparison detects mark differences even though underlying values are identical\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe core fix requires synchronizing the three stages to use the same mark-application logic:\n\n1. **Apply Schema Marks During State Deserialization** - NOT just during expression evaluation:\n   - In `instance_object_src.Decode()`, after unmarking and remarking with `AttrSensitivePaths`, apply schema marks unconditionally\n   - This ensures that state values always carry complete mark information\n\n2. **Persist Complete Marks to State** - Include schema marks in serialization:\n   - Before encoding state in `instance_object.Encode()`, compute and include schema marks in addition to variable-reference marks\n   - This requires passing the schema to the encode operation (currently it doesn't have access)\n\n3. **Alternative: Skip Mark Comparison for NoOp Actions**:\n   - Remove or modify the check at line 1208 that triggers updates based on mark differences alone\n   - Only treat as Update if actual value changes, not mark-only differences (already done for UnmarkDeep at line 1049-1052)\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Check state file's `sensitive_attributes` section:\n   - Should include paths for ALL schema-defined `Sensitive: true` attributes\n   - Not just those from variable references\n\n2. Compare before/after sensitivity in plan:\n   - `terraform plan -json` should show schema-defined attributes in `sensitive_values`\n\n3. Verify evaluator marks match persistence:\n   - Schema marks applied in `GetResource()` should match marks in state\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\nThis issue affects:\n- Any provider with schema attributes marked `Sensitive: true`\n- User confidence in plan accuracy (false positives)\n- State file accuracy (incomplete sensitivity information)\n- JSON output completeness (missing sensitivity metadata)\n\nThe fix would require careful coordination between:\n- State serialization/deserialization layer\n- Plan generation layer\n- Provider schema application layer\n- Expression evaluation layer\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":293,"cache_read_input_tokens":99464,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":293},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b6b1d350-4873-4907-9a27-826c478b5f05","uuid":"67865418-69c3-4798-9612-0410b40dec1f"}
